\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
A plottable representing a graph in a plot. 



Usually you create new graphs by calling \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b}{QCustom\+Plot\+::add\+Graph}. The resulting instance can be accessed via \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a6ecae130f684b25276fb47bd3a5875c6_a6ecae130f684b25276fb47bd3a5875c6}{QCustom\+Plot\+::graph}.

To plot data, assign it with the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a1eae9429a316b008e2d99b2d65a54395_a1eae9429a316b008e2d99b2d65a54395}{set\+Data} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f}{add\+Data} functions. Alternatively, you can also access and modify the data via the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a141aa31a1f19bbd0ce60f55eaeb9ea60_a141aa31a1f19bbd0ce60f55eaeb9ea60}{data} method, which returns a pointer to the internal \doxylink{qcustomplot_8h_a9acaec6c7811dbc3f9ca07b6631f0442_a9acaec6c7811dbc3f9ca07b6631f0442}{QCPGraph\+Data\+Container}.

Graphs are used to display single-\/valued data. Single-\/valued means that there should only be one data point per unique key coordinate. In other words, the graph can\textquotesingle{}t have {\itshape loops}. If you do want to plot non-\/single-\/valued curves, rather use the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_curve}{QCPCurve} plottable.

Gaps in the graph line can be created by adding data points with NaN as value ({\ttfamily q\+QNa\+N()} or {\ttfamily std\+::numeric\+\_\+limits$<$double$>$\+::quiet\+\_\+\+Na\+N()}) in between the two data points that shall be separated.\hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_qcpgraph-appearance}{}\doxysubsection{\texorpdfstring{Changing the appearance}{Changing the appearance}}\label{class_q_c_p_graph_qcpgraph-appearance}
The appearance of the graph is mainly determined by the line style, scatter style, brush and pen of the graph (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a513fecccff5b2a50ce53f665338c60ff_a513fecccff5b2a50ce53f665338c60ff}{set\+Line\+Style}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a12bd17a8ba21983163ec5d8f42a9fea5_a12bd17a8ba21983163ec5d8f42a9fea5}{set\+Scatter\+Style}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74}{set\+Brush}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ab74b09ae4c0e7e13142fe4b5bf46cac7_ab74b09ae4c0e7e13142fe4b5bf46cac7}{set\+Pen}).\hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_filling}{}\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Filling under or between graphs}{Filling under or between graphs}}\label{class_q_c_p_graph_filling}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} knows two types of fills\+: Normal graph fills towards the zero-\/value-\/line parallel to the key axis of the graph, and fills between two graphs, called channel fills. To enable a fill, just set a brush with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74}{set\+Brush} which is neither Qt\+::\+No\+Brush nor fully transparent.

By default, a normal fill towards the zero-\/value-\/line will be drawn. To set up a channel fill between this graph and another one, call \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a2d03156df1b64037a2e36cfa50351ca3_a2d03156df1b64037a2e36cfa50351ca3}{set\+Channel\+Fill\+Graph} with the other graph as parameter.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b}{QCustom\+Plot\+::add\+Graph}, \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a6ecae130f684b25276fb47bd3a5875c6_a6ecae130f684b25276fb47bd3a5875c6}{QCustom\+Plot\+::graph} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxysubsection{Constructor \& Destructor Documentation}
\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{QCPGraph()}{QCPGraph()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c} 
QCPGraph\+::\+QCPGraph (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis}{QCPAxis}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{key\+Axis}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis}{QCPAxis}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{value\+Axis}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [explicit]}}

Constructs a graph which uses {\itshape key\+Axis} as its key axis ("{}x"{}) and {\itshape value\+Axis} as its value axis ("{}y"{}). {\itshape key\+Axis} and {\itshape value\+Axis} must reside in the same \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} instance and not have the same orientation. If either of these restrictions is violated, a corresponding message is printed to the debug output (q\+Debug), the construction is not aborted, though.

The created \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} is automatically registered with the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} instance inferred from {\itshape key\+Axis}. This \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} instance takes ownership of the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph}, so do not delete it manually but use \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_af3dafd56884208474f311d6226513ab2_af3dafd56884208474f311d6226513ab2}{QCustom\+Plot\+::remove\+Plottable()} instead.

To directly create a graph inside a plot, you can also use the simpler \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b}{QCustom\+Plot\+::add\+Graph} function. Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{class_q_c_p_graph_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c_a0393a38cf7183cbf46348eb6cf9a5a6c_cgraph}
\end{center}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!addData@{addData}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{addData()}{addData()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f} 
void QCPGraph\+::add\+Data (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QVector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{keys}{, }\item[{const QVector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{values}{, }\item[{bool}]{already\+Sorted}{ = {\ttfamily false}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Adds the provided points in {\itshape keys} and {\itshape values} to the current data. The provided vectors should have equal length. Else, the number of added points will be the size of the smallest vector.

If you can guarantee that the passed data points are sorted by {\itshape keys} in ascending order, you can set {\itshape already\+Sorted} to true, to improve performance by saving a sorting run.

Alternatively, you can also access and modify the data directly via the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a141aa31a1f19bbd0ce60f55eaeb9ea60_a141aa31a1f19bbd0ce60f55eaeb9ea60}{data} method, which returns a pointer to the internal data container. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{class_q_c_p_graph_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f_ae0555c0d3fe0fa7cb8628f88158d420f_icgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_aa64e93cb5b606d8110d2cc0a349bb30f_aa64e93cb5b606d8110d2cc0a349bb30f}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!addToLegend@{addToLegend}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_aa64e93cb5b606d8110d2cc0a349bb30f_aa64e93cb5b606d8110d2cc0a349bb30f} 
bool QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::add\+To\+Legend (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_legend}{QCPLegend}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{legend}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Adds this plottable to the specified {\itshape legend}.

Creates a \doxylink{class_q_c_p_plottable_legend_item}{QCPPlottable\+Legend\+Item} which is inserted into the legend. Returns true on success, i.\+e. when the legend exists and a legend item associated with this plottable isn\textquotesingle{}t already in the legend.

If the plottable needs a more specialized representation in the legend, you can create a corresponding subclass of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_plottable_legend_item}{QCPPlottable\+Legend\+Item} and add it to the legend manually instead of calling this method.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{coordsToPixels()}{coordsToPixels()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7ad84a36472441cf1f555c5683d0da93_a7ad84a36472441cf1f555c5683d0da93} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::coords\+To\+Pixels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{key}{, }\item[{double}]{value}{, }\item[{double \&}]{x}{, }\item[{double \&}]{y}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Convenience function for transforming a key/value pair to pixels on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} surface, taking the orientations of the axes associated with this plottable into account (e.\+g. whether key represents x or y).

{\itshape key} and {\itshape value} are transformed to the coodinates in pixels and are written to {\itshape x} and {\itshape y}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6ca0699a6af5f25a7565de7c50ce13b2_a6ca0699a6af5f25a7565de7c50ce13b2}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!dataPixelPosition@{dataPixelPosition}}
\index{dataPixelPosition@{dataPixelPosition}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{dataPixelPosition()}{dataPixelPosition()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6ca0699a6af5f25a7565de7c50ce13b2_a6ca0699a6af5f25a7565de7c50ce13b2} 
QPointF \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::data\+Pixel\+Position (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{index}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}





Returns the pixel position on the widget surface at which the data point at the given {\itshape index} appears.

Usually this corresponds to the point of data\+Main\+Key/ data\+Main\+Value, in pixel coordinates. However, depending on the plottable, this might be a different apparent position than just a coord-\/to-\/pixel transform of those values. For example, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} apparent data values can be shifted depending on their stacking, bar grouping or configured base value.    

Implements \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_plottable_interface1_d_a35fd032c6e5226ff7b50e0f37c57922b_a35fd032c6e5226ff7b50e0f37c57922b}{QCPPlottable\+Interface1D}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!drawPolyline@{drawPolyline}}
\index{drawPolyline@{drawPolyline}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{drawPolyline()}{drawPolyline()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206} 
void \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::draw\+Polyline (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_painter}{QCPPainter}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{painter}{, }\item[{const QVector$<$ QPointF $>$ \&}]{line\+Data}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

A helper method which draws a line with the passed {\itshape painter}, according to the pixel data in {\itshape line\+Data}. NaN points create gaps in the line, as expected from \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot}\textquotesingle{}s plottables (this is the main difference to QPainter\textquotesingle{}s regular draw\+Polyline, which handles Na\+Ns by lagging or crashing).

Further it uses a faster line drawing technique based on \doxylink{class_q_c_p_painter_a0b4b1b9bd495e182c731774dc800e6e0_a0b4b1b9bd495e182c731774dc800e6e0}{QCPPainter\+::draw\+Line} rather than {\ttfamily QPainter\+::draw\+Polyline} if the configured \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a94a33cbdadbbac5934843508bcfc210d_a94a33cbdadbbac5934843508bcfc210d}{QCustom\+Plot\+::set\+Plotting\+Hints()} and {\itshape painter} style allows. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:
\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206_a7adc6c3cccebb5341f11e0c2b7d54206_icgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_abeb0bbe81026c024bf3d508d13cf5e0e_abeb0bbe81026c024bf3d508d13cf5e0e}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!drawScatterPlot@{drawScatterPlot}}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!findBegin@{findBegin}}
\index{findBegin@{findBegin}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{findBegin()}{findBegin()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6} 
int \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::find\+Begin (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{sort\+Key}{, }\item[{bool}]{expanded\+Range}{ = {\ttfamily true}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}





Returns the index of the data point with a (sort-\/)key that is equal to, just below, or just above {\itshape sort\+Key}. If {\itshape expanded\+Range} is true, the data point just below {\itshape sort\+Key} will be considered, otherwise the one just above.

This can be used in conjunction with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a}{find\+End} to iterate over data points within a given key range, including or excluding the bounding data points that are just beyond the specified range.

If {\itshape expanded\+Range} is true but there are no data points below {\itshape sort\+Key}, 0 is returned.

If the container is empty, returns 0 (in that case, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a}{find\+End} will also return 0, so a loop using these methods will not iterate over the index 0).

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a}{find\+End}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_container_a2ad8a5399072d99a242d3a6d2d7e278a_a2ad8a5399072d99a242d3a6d2d7e278a}{QCPData\+Container\+::find\+Begin}    
\end{DoxySeeAlso}


Implements \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_plottable_interface1_d_ac8f224af7f2afeed46d82368344d8d9e_ac8f224af7f2afeed46d82368344d8d9e}{QCPPlottable\+Interface1D}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!findEnd@{findEnd}}
\index{findEnd@{findEnd}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{findEnd()}{findEnd()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a_a6e3ba20c9160d7361e58070390d10b1a} 
int \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::find\+End (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{sort\+Key}{, }\item[{bool}]{expanded\+Range}{ = {\ttfamily true}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}





Returns the index one after the data point with a (sort-\/)key that is equal to, just above, or just below {\itshape sort\+Key}. If {\itshape expanded\+Range} is true, the data point just above {\itshape sort\+Key} will be considered, otherwise the one just below.

This can be used in conjunction with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6}{find\+Begin} to iterate over data points within a given key range, including the bounding data points that are just below and above the specified range.

If {\itshape expanded\+Range} is true but there are no data points above {\itshape sort\+Key}, the index just above the highest data point is returned.

If the container is empty, returns 0.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6_ad0b46d25cde3d035b180fb8f10c056e6}{find\+Begin}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_container_afb8b8f23cc2b7234a793a25ce79fe48f_afb8b8f23cc2b7234a793a25ce79fe48f}{QCPData\+Container\+::find\+End}    
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

void \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::get\+Data\+Segments (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QList$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_range}{QCPData\+Range}} $>$ \&}]{selected\+Segments}{, }\item[{QList$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_range}{QCPData\+Range}} $>$ \&}]{unselected\+Segments}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Splits all data into selected and unselected segments and outputs them via {\itshape selected\+Segments} and {\itshape unselected\+Segments}, respectively.

This is useful when subclasses implement their \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a2b0849598f06e834b43ce18cd13bcdc3_a2b0849598f06e834b43ce18cd13bcdc3}{draw} method and need to draw selected segments with a different pen/brush than unselected segments (also see \doxylink{class_q_c_p_selection_decorator}{QCPSelection\+Decorator}).

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_aac47c6189e3aea46ea46939e5d14796c_aac47c6189e3aea46ea46939e5d14796c}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!getKeyRange@{getKeyRange}}
\index{getKeyRange@{getKeyRange}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getKeyRange()}{getKeyRange()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_aac47c6189e3aea46ea46939e5d14796c_aac47c6189e3aea46ea46939e5d14796c} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}} QCPGraph\+::get\+Key\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool \&}]{found\+Range}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9}{QCP\+::\+Sign\+Domain}}}]{in\+Sign\+Domain}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9aa38352ef02d51ddfa4399d9551566e24}{QCP\+::sd\+Both}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}}

Returns the coordinate range that all data in this plottable span in the key axis dimension. For logarithmic plots, one can set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to either \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a2d18af0bc58f6528d1e82ce699fe4829}{QCP\+::sd\+Negative} or \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a584784b75fb816abcc627cf743bb699f}{QCP\+::sd\+Positive} in order to restrict the returned range to that sign domain. E.\+g. when only negative range is wanted, set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a2d18af0bc58f6528d1e82ce699fe4829}{QCP\+::sd\+Negative} and all positive points will be ignored for range calculation. For no restriction, just set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9aa38352ef02d51ddfa4399d9551566e24}{QCP\+::sd\+Both} (default). {\itshape found\+Range} is an output parameter that indicates whether a range could be found or not. If this is false, you shouldn\textquotesingle{}t use the returned range (e.\+g. no points in data).

Note that {\itshape found\+Range} is not the same as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0}{QCPRange\+::valid\+Range}, since the range returned by this function may have size zero (e.\+g. when there is only one data point). In this case {\itshape found\+Range} would return true, but the returned range is not a valid range in terms of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0}{QCPRange\+::valid\+Range}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_a8f773e56f191a61c06e129e90a604d77_a8f773e56f191a61c06e129e90a604d77}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!getValueRange@{getValueRange}}
\index{getValueRange@{getValueRange}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getValueRange()}{getValueRange()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_a8f773e56f191a61c06e129e90a604d77_a8f773e56f191a61c06e129e90a604d77} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}} QCPGraph\+::get\+Value\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool \&}]{found\+Range}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9}{QCP\+::\+Sign\+Domain}}}]{in\+Sign\+Domain}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9aa38352ef02d51ddfa4399d9551566e24}{QCP\+::sd\+Both}}}, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}} \&}]{in\+Key\+Range}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}}()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}}

Returns the coordinate range that the data points in the specified key range ({\itshape in\+Key\+Range}) span in the value axis dimension. For logarithmic plots, one can set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to either \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a2d18af0bc58f6528d1e82ce699fe4829}{QCP\+::sd\+Negative} or \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a584784b75fb816abcc627cf743bb699f}{QCP\+::sd\+Positive} in order to restrict the returned range to that sign domain. E.\+g. when only negative range is wanted, set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9a2d18af0bc58f6528d1e82ce699fe4829}{QCP\+::sd\+Negative} and all positive points will be ignored for range calculation. For no restriction, just set {\itshape in\+Sign\+Domain} to \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9_afd50e7cf431af385614987d8553ff8a9aa38352ef02d51ddfa4399d9551566e24}{QCP\+::sd\+Both} (default). {\itshape found\+Range} is an output parameter that indicates whether a range could be found or not. If this is false, you shouldn\textquotesingle{}t use the returned range (e.\+g. no points in data).

If {\itshape in\+Key\+Range} has both lower and upper bound set to zero (is equal to {\ttfamily \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange()}}), all data points are considered, without any restriction on the keys.

Note that {\itshape found\+Range} is not the same as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0}{QCPRange\+::valid\+Range}, since the range returned by this function may have size zero (e.\+g. when there is only one data point). In this case {\itshape found\+Range} would return true, but the returned range is not a valid range in terms of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0_ab38bd4841c77c7bb86c9eea0f142dcc0}{QCPRange\+::valid\+Range}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_a8599447a7f8cbbdcf0b94edcc11df560_a8599447a7f8cbbdcf0b94edcc11df560}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!getVisibleDataBounds@{getVisibleDataBounds}}
\index{getVisibleDataBounds@{getVisibleDataBounds}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getVisibleDataBounds()}{getVisibleDataBounds()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_a8599447a7f8cbbdcf0b94edcc11df560_a8599447a7f8cbbdcf0b94edcc11df560} 
void QCPGraph\+::get\+Visible\+Data\+Bounds (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_container_a92fefe78f22b5a625edc773f69a5c798_a92fefe78f22b5a625edc773f69a5c798}{QCPGraph\+Data\+Container\+::const\+\_\+iterator}} \&}]{begin}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_container_a92fefe78f22b5a625edc773f69a5c798_a92fefe78f22b5a625edc773f69a5c798}{QCPGraph\+Data\+Container\+::const\+\_\+iterator}} \&}]{end}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_range}{QCPData\+Range}} \&}]{range\+Restriction}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

This method outputs the currently visible data range via {\itshape begin} and {\itshape end}. The returned range will also never exceed {\itshape range\+Restriction}.

This method takes into account that the drawing of data lines at the axis rect border always requires the points just outside the visible axis range. So {\itshape begin} and {\itshape end} may actually indicate a range that contains one additional data point to the left and right of the visible axis range. \Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_ac3e6f4b3387338df45992b47691b2551_ac3e6f4b3387338df45992b47691b2551}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!lineStyle@{lineStyle}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_ac3e6f4b3387338df45992b47691b2551_ac3e6f4b3387338df45992b47691b2551} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_ad60175cd9b5cac937c5ee685c32c0859_ad60175cd9b5cac937c5ee685c32c0859}{Line\+Style}} QCPGraph\+::line\+Style (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!mouseDoubleClickEvent@{mouseDoubleClickEvent}}
\index{mouseDoubleClickEvent@{mouseDoubleClickEvent}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseDoubleClickEvent()}{mouseDoubleClickEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81} 
void QCPLayerable\+::mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QVariant \&}]{details}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user presses the mouse button a second time in a double-\/click, while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test}.

The \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event} is called instead of the second \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}. So in the case of a double-\/click, the event succession is {\itshape press\+Event -- release\+Event -- double\+Click\+Event -- release\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape details} contains layerable-\/specific details about the hit, which were generated in the previous call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test}. For example, One-\/dimensional plottables like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} convey the clicked data point in the {\itshape details} parameter, as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection} packed as QVariant. Multi-\/part objects convey the specific {\ttfamily Selectable\+Part} that was hit (e.\+g. \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f}{QCPAxis\+::\+Selectable\+Part} in the case of axes).

Similarly to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, once a layerable has accepted the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, it is considered the mouse grabber and will receive all following calls to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}{mouse\+Move\+Event} and \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}{mouse\+Release\+Event} for this mouse interaction (a "{}mouse interaction"{} in this context ends with the release).

The default implementation does nothing except explicitly ignoring the event with {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}{mouse\+Move\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}


Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_text_element_a2272ff775ab385f612e9fd39773de7c0_a2272ff775ab385f612e9fd39773de7c0}{QCPText\+Element}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!mouseMoveEvent@{mouseMoveEvent}}
\index{mouseMoveEvent@{mouseMoveEvent}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseMoveEvent()}{mouseMoveEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4} 
void QCPLayerable\+::mouse\+Move\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QPointF \&}]{start\+Pos}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user moves the mouse while holding a mouse button, after this layerable has become the mouse grabber by accepting the preceding \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape start\+Pos} indicates the position where the initial \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event} occurred, that started the mouse interaction.

The default implementation does nothing.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}


Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis_ac5a269609e6177737faabdc46434d8c7_ac5a269609e6177737faabdc46434d8c7}{QCPAxis}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis_rect_a9cd27ad8c5cfb49aefd9dbb30def4beb_a9cd27ad8c5cfb49aefd9dbb30def4beb}{QCPAxis\+Rect}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_color_scale_a3b2bd79725aefaf2630fc76e90939442_a3b2bd79725aefaf2630fc76e90939442}{QCPColor\+Scale}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_color_scale_axis_rect_private_a9cd27ad8c5cfb49aefd9dbb30def4beb_a9cd27ad8c5cfb49aefd9dbb30def4beb}{QCPColor\+Scale\+Axis\+Rect\+Private}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_angular_a5e2b49c56b57abc2ac2005e330ef1ee7_a5e2b49c56b57abc2ac2005e330ef1ee7}{QCPPolar\+Axis\+Angular}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!mousePressEvent@{mousePressEvent}}
\index{mousePressEvent@{mousePressEvent}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mousePressEvent()}{mousePressEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376} 
void QCPLayerable\+::mouse\+Press\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QVariant \&}]{details}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user presses a mouse button while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape details} contains layerable-\/specific details about the hit, which were generated in the previous call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test}. For example, One-\/dimensional plottables like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} convey the clicked data point in the {\itshape details} parameter, as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection} packed as QVariant. Multi-\/part objects convey the specific {\ttfamily Selectable\+Part} that was hit (e.\+g. \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f}{QCPAxis\+::\+Selectable\+Part} in the case of axes).

\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} uses an event propagation system that works the same as Qt\textquotesingle{}s system. If your layerable doesn\textquotesingle{}t reimplement the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event} or explicitly calls {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()} in its reimplementation, the event will be propagated to the next layerable in the stacking order.

Once a layerable has accepted the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, it is considered the mouse grabber and will receive all following calls to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}{mouse\+Move\+Event} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}{mouse\+Release\+Event} for this mouse interaction (a "{}mouse interaction"{} in this context ends with the release).

The default implementation does nothing except explicitly ignoring the event with {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}{mouse\+Move\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!mouseReleaseEvent@{mouseReleaseEvent}}
\index{mouseReleaseEvent@{mouseReleaseEvent}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseReleaseEvent()}{mouseReleaseEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c_aa0d79b005686f668622bbe66ac03ba2c} 
void QCPLayerable\+::mouse\+Release\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QPointF \&}]{start\+Pos}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user releases the mouse button, after this layerable has become the mouse grabber by accepting the preceding \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape start\+Pos} indicates the position where the initial \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376_af6567604818db90f4fd52822f8bc8376}{mouse\+Press\+Event} occurred, that started the mouse interaction.

The default implementation does nothing.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!parentLayerable@{parentLayerable}}
\index{parentLayerable@{parentLayerable}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{parentLayerable()}{parentLayerable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_layerable}{QCPLayerable}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} QCPLayerable\+::parent\+Layerable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Returns the parent layerable of this layerable. The parent layerable is used to provide visibility hierarchies in conjunction with the method \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7}{real\+Visibility}. This way, layerables only get drawn if their parent layerables are visible, too.

Note that a parent layerable is not necessarily also the QObject parent for memory management. Further, a layerable doesn\textquotesingle{}t always have a parent layerable, so this function may return {\ttfamily nullptr}.

A parent layerable is set implicitly when placed inside layout elements and doesn\textquotesingle{}t need to be set manually by the user. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858_icgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a3903c1120ab5c27e7fa46b597ef267bd_a3903c1120ab5c27e7fa46b597ef267bd}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!pixelsToCoords@{pixelsToCoords}}
\index{pixelsToCoords@{pixelsToCoords}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pixelsToCoords()}{pixelsToCoords()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a3903c1120ab5c27e7fa46b597ef267bd_a3903c1120ab5c27e7fa46b597ef267bd} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::pixels\+To\+Coords (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{x}{, }\item[{double}]{y}{, }\item[{double \&}]{key}{, }\item[{double \&}]{value}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Convenience function for transforming a x/y pixel pair on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} surface to plot coordinates, taking the orientations of the axes associated with this plottable into account (e.\+g. whether key represents x or y).

{\itshape x} and {\itshape y} are transformed to the plot coodinates and are written to {\itshape key} and {\itshape value}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!realVisibility@{realVisibility}}
\index{realVisibility@{realVisibility}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{realVisibility()}{realVisibility()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7} 
bool QCPLayerable\+::real\+Visibility (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Returns whether this layerable is visible, taking the visibility of the layerable parent and the visibility of this layerable\textquotesingle{}s layer into account. This is the method that is consulted to decide whether a layerable shall be drawn or not.

If this layerable has a direct layerable parent (usually set via hierarchies implemented in subclasses, like in the case of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layout_element}{QCPLayout\+Element}), this function returns true only if this layerable has its visibility set to true and the parent layerable\textquotesingle{}s \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7}{real\+Visibility} returns true. \Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a3cc235007e2343a65ad4f463767e0e20_a3cc235007e2343a65ad4f463767e0e20}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!removeFromLegend@{removeFromLegend}}
\index{removeFromLegend@{removeFromLegend}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{removeFromLegend()}{removeFromLegend()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a3cc235007e2343a65ad4f463767e0e20_a3cc235007e2343a65ad4f463767e0e20} 
bool QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::remove\+From\+Legend (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_legend}{QCPLegend}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{legend}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Removes the plottable from the specifed {\itshape legend}. This means the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_plottable_legend_item}{QCPPlottable\+Legend\+Item} that is associated with this plottable is removed.

Returns true on success, i.\+e. if the legend exists and a legend item associated with this plottable was found and removed.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a1491c4a606bccd2d09e65e11b79eb882_a1491c4a606bccd2d09e65e11b79eb882}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!rescaleAxes@{rescaleAxes}}
\index{rescaleAxes@{rescaleAxes}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rescaleAxes()}{rescaleAxes()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a1491c4a606bccd2d09e65e11b79eb882_a1491c4a606bccd2d09e65e11b79eb882} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::rescale\+Axes (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{only\+Enlarge}{ = {\ttfamily false}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Rescales the key and value axes associated with this plottable to contain all displayed data, so the whole plottable is visible. If the scaling of an axis is logarithmic, rescale\+Axes will make sure not to rescale to an illegal range i.\+e. a range containing different signs and/or zero. Instead it will stay in the current sign domain and ignore all parts of the plottable that lie outside of that domain.

{\itshape only\+Enlarge} makes sure the ranges are only expanded, never reduced. So it\textquotesingle{}s possible to show multiple plottables in their entirety by multiple calls to rescale\+Axes where the first call has {\itshape only\+Enlarge} set to false (the default), and all subsequent set to true.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a714eaf36b12434cd71846215504db82e_a714eaf36b12434cd71846215504db82e} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::rescale\+Value\+Axis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{only\+Enlarge}{ = {\ttfamily false}, }\item[{bool}]{in\+Key\+Range}{ = {\ttfamily false}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Rescales the value axis of the plottable so the whole plottable is visible. If {\itshape in\+Key\+Range} is set to true, only the data points which are in the currently visible key axis range are considered.

Returns true if the axis was actually scaled. This might not be the case if this plottable has an invalid range, e.\+g. because it has no data points.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setAdaptiveSampling@{setAdaptiveSampling}}
\index{setAdaptiveSampling@{setAdaptiveSampling}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setAdaptiveSampling()}{setAdaptiveSampling()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c} 
void QCPGraph\+::set\+Adaptive\+Sampling (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{enabled}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets whether adaptive sampling shall be used when plotting this graph. \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot}\textquotesingle{}s adaptive sampling technique can drastically improve the replot performance for graphs with a larger number of points (e.\+g. above 10,000), without notably changing the appearance of the graph.

By default, adaptive sampling is enabled. Even if enabled, \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} decides whether adaptive sampling shall actually be used on a per-\/graph basis. So leaving adaptive sampling enabled has no disadvantage in almost all cases.



As can be seen, line plots experience no visual degradation from adaptive sampling. Outliers are reproduced reliably, as well as the overall shape of the data set. The replot time reduces dramatically though. This allows \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} to display large amounts of data in realtime.



Care must be taken when using high-\/density scatter plots in combination with adaptive sampling. The adaptive sampling algorithm treats scatter plots more carefully than line plots which still gives a significant reduction of replot times, but not quite as much as for line plots. This is because scatter plots inherently need more data points to be preserved in order to still resemble the original, non-\/adaptive-\/sampling plot. As shown above, the results still aren\textquotesingle{}t quite identical, as banding occurs for the outer data points. This is in fact intentional, such that the boundaries of the data cloud stay visible to the viewer. How strong the banding appears, depends on the point density, i.\+e. the number of points in the plot.

For some situations with scatter plots it might thus be desirable to manually turn adaptive sampling off. For example, when saving the plot to disk. This can be achieved by setting {\itshape enabled} to false before issuing a command like \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_ac92cc9256d12f354b40a4be4600b5fb9_ac92cc9256d12f354b40a4be4600b5fb9}{QCustom\+Plot\+::save\+Png}, and setting {\itshape enabled} back to true afterwards. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak
\begin{figure}[H]
\begin{center}
\leavevmode
\includegraphics[width=350pt]{class_q_c_p_graph_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c_ab468cd600160f327836aa0644291e64c_icgraph}
\end{center}
\end{figure}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74_a7a4b92144dca6453a1f0f210e27edc74} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Brush (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QBrush \&}]{brush}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

The brush is used to draw basic fills of the plottable representation in the plot. The Fill can be a color, gradient or texture, see the usage of QBrush.

For example, the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} subclass draws the fill under the graph with this brush, when it\textquotesingle{}s not set to Qt\+::\+No\+Brush.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_a73578d786532132310a926c3cd529b29_a73578d786532132310a926c3cd529b29}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setData@{setData}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_a73578d786532132310a926c3cd529b29_a73578d786532132310a926c3cd529b29} 
void QCPGraph\+::set\+Data (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QVector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{keys}{, }\item[{const QVector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{values}{, }\item[{bool}]{already\+Sorted}{ = {\ttfamily false}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Replaces the current data with the provided points in {\itshape keys} and {\itshape values}. The provided vectors should have equal length. Else, the number of added points will be the size of the smallest vector.

If you can guarantee that the passed data points are sorted by {\itshape keys} in ascending order, you can set {\itshape already\+Sorted} to true, to improve performance by saving a sorting run.

Replaces the current data container with the provided {\itshape data} container.

Since a QShared\+Pointer is used, multiple QCPGraphs may share the same data container safely. Modifying the data in the container will then affect all graphs that share the container. Sharing can be achieved by simply exchanging the data containers wrapped in shared pointers\+:

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setKeyAxis@{setKeyAxis}}
\index{setKeyAxis@{setKeyAxis}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setKeyAxis()}{setKeyAxis()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Key\+Axis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis}{QCPAxis}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{axis}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

The key axis of a plottable can be set to any axis of a \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot}, as long as it is orthogonal to the plottable\textquotesingle{}s value axis. This function performs no checks to make sure this is the case. The typical mathematical choice is to use the x-\/axis (\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a968b5ac86c181a49bba78c2b62a80cb3_a968b5ac86c181a49bba78c2b62a80cb3}{QCustom\+Plot\+::x\+Axis}) as key axis and the y-\/axis (\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_af6fea5679725b152c14facd920b19367_af6fea5679725b152c14facd920b19367}{QCustom\+Plot\+::y\+Axis}) as value axis.

Normally, the key and value axes are set in the constructor of the plottable (or \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b}{QCustom\+Plot\+::add\+Graph} when working with QCPGraphs through the dedicated graph interface).

bool QCPLayerable\+::set\+Layer (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_layer}{QCPLayer}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{layer}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Sets the {\itshape layer} of this layerable object. The object will be placed on top of the other objects already on {\itshape layer}.

If {\itshape layer} is 0, this layerable will not be on any layer and thus not appear in the plot (or interact/receive events).

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_graph_a17cebd3196f434258abb82ba6dc443f2_a17cebd3196f434258abb82ba6dc443f2}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setScatterSkip@{setScatterSkip}}
\index{setScatterSkip@{setScatterSkip}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setScatterSkip()}{setScatterSkip()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_graph_a17cebd3196f434258abb82ba6dc443f2_a17cebd3196f434258abb82ba6dc443f2} 
void QCPGraph\+::set\+Scatter\+Skip (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{skip}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

If scatters are displayed (scatter style not \doxylink{class_q_c_p_scatter_style_adb31525af6b680e6f1b7472e43859349_adb31525af6b680e6f1b7472e43859349abd144c291ca274f77053ec68cab6c022}{QCPScatter\+Style\+::ss\+None}), {\itshape skip} number of scatter points are skipped/not drawn after every drawn scatter point.

This can be used to make the data appear sparser while for example still having a smooth line, and to improve performance for very high density plots.

If {\itshape skip} is set to 0 (default), all scatter points are drawn.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_a12bd17a8ba21983163ec5d8f42a9fea5_a12bd17a8ba21983163ec5d8f42a9fea5}{set\+Scatter\+Style}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setSelectable@{setSelectable}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setSelectable()}{setSelectable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Selectable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_q_c_p_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038}{QCP\+::\+Selection\+Type}}}]{selectable}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Sets whether and to which granularity this plottable can be selected.

A selection can happen by clicking on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} surface (When \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5}{QCustom\+Plot\+::set\+Interactions} contains \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_a2ad6bb6281c7c2d593d4277b44c2b037_a2ad6bb6281c7c2d593d4277b44c2b037a67148c8227b4155eca49135fc274c7ec}{QCP\+::i\+Select\+Plottables}), by dragging a selection rect (When \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a810ef958ebe84db661c7288b526c0deb_a810ef958ebe84db661c7288b526c0deb}{QCustom\+Plot\+::set\+Selection\+Rect\+Mode} is \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_ac9aa4d6d81ac76b094f9af9ad2d3aacf_ac9aa4d6d81ac76b094f9af9ad2d3aacfa62c286e8da283a0cbb88ecac2f3f7506}{QCP\+::srm\+Select}), or programmatically by calling \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436}{set\+Selection}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436}{set\+Selection}, \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038}{QCP\+::\+Selection\+Type}

\end{center}
\end{figure}
\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setSelection@{setSelection}}
\index{setSelection@{setSelection}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setSelection()}{setSelection()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436_a219bc5403a9d85d3129165ec3f5ae436} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Selection (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection}}}]{selection}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Sets which data ranges of this plottable are selected. Selected data ranges are drawn differently (e.\+g. color) in the plot. This can be controlled via the selection decorator (see \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7861518e47ca0c6a0c386032c2db075e_a7861518e47ca0c6a0c386032c2db075e}{selection\+Decorator}).

The entire selection mechanism for plottables is handled automatically when \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5}{QCustom\+Plot\+::set\+Interactions} contains i\+Select\+Plottables. You only need to call this function when you wish to change the selection state programmatically.

Using \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3}{set\+Selectable} you can further specify for each plottable whether and to which granularity it is selectable. If {\itshape selection} is not compatible with the current \doxylink{namespace_q_c_p_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038_ac6cb9db26a564b27feda362a438db038}{QCP\+::\+Selection\+Type} set via \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3}{set\+Selectable}, the resulting selection will be adjusted accordingly (see \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection_a17b84d852911531d229f4a76aa239a75_a17b84d852911531d229f4a76aa239a75}{QCPData\+Selection\+::enforce\+Type}).

emits the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a3af66432b1dca93b28e00e78a8c7c1d9_a3af66432b1dca93b28e00e78a8c7c1d9}{selection\+Changed} signal when {\itshape selected} is different from the previous selection state.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3_ac238d6e910f976f1f30d41c2bca44ac3}{set\+Selectable}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Selection\+Decorator (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_selection_decorator}{QCPSelection\+Decorator}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{decorator}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Use this method to set an own \doxylink{class_q_c_p_selection_decorator}{QCPSelection\+Decorator} (subclass) instance. This allows you to customize the visual representation of selected data ranges further than by using the default \doxylink{class_q_c_p_selection_decorator}{QCPSelection\+Decorator}.

The plottable takes ownership of the {\itshape decorator}.

The currently set decorator can be accessed via \doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a7861518e47ca0c6a0c386032c2db075e_a7861518e47ca0c6a0c386032c2db075e}{selection\+Decorator}. Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a71626a07367e241ec62ad2c34baf21cb_a71626a07367e241ec62ad2c34baf21cb}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setValueAxis@{setValueAxis}}
\index{setValueAxis@{setValueAxis}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setValueAxis()}{setValueAxis()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a71626a07367e241ec62ad2c34baf21cb_a71626a07367e241ec62ad2c34baf21cb} 
void QCPAbstract\+Plottable\+::set\+Value\+Axis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis}{QCPAxis}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{axis}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

The value axis of a plottable can be set to any axis of a \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot}, as long as it is orthogonal to the plottable\textquotesingle{}s key axis. This function performs no checks to make sure this is the case. The typical mathematical choice is to use the x-\/axis (\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a968b5ac86c181a49bba78c2b62a80cb3_a968b5ac86c181a49bba78c2b62a80cb3}{QCustom\+Plot\+::x\+Axis}) as key axis and the y-\/axis (\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_af6fea5679725b152c14facd920b19367_af6fea5679725b152c14facd920b19367}{QCustom\+Plot\+::y\+Axis}) as value axis.

Normally, the key and value axes are set in the constructor of the plottable (or \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b_a2836a46e31d5aee174ae054c0aa6580b}{QCustom\+Plot\+::add\+Graph} when working with QCPGraphs through the dedicated graph interface).

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920_a8524fa2994c63c0913ebd9bb2ffa3920}{set\+Key\+Axis} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_a3bed99ddc396b48ce3ebfdc0418744f8_a3bed99ddc396b48ce3ebfdc0418744f8}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!setVisible@{setVisible}}

Sets the visibility of this layerable object. If an object is not visible, it will not be drawn on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} surface, and user interaction with it (e.\+g. click and selection) is not possible. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_afe0d56e39cc076032922f059b304c092_afe0d56e39cc076032922f059b304c092}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!sortKeyIsMainKey@{sortKeyIsMainKey}}
\index{sortKeyIsMainKey@{sortKeyIsMainKey}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sortKeyIsMainKey()}{sortKeyIsMainKey()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_afe0d56e39cc076032922f059b304c092_afe0d56e39cc076032922f059b304c092} 
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_graph_data}{QCPGraph\+Data}} $>$\+::sort\+Key\+Is\+Main\+Key (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}





Returns whether the sort key (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_aa8277da921b009bce474437d50b4a2d8_aa8277da921b009bce474437d50b4a2d8}{data\+Sort\+Key}) is identical to the main key (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d_aeb156ebf5d3c8de906b428be30733ad8_aeb156ebf5d3c8de906b428be30733ad8}{data\+Main\+Key}).

What the sort and main keys are, is defined by the plottable\textquotesingle{}s data type. See the \doxysectlink{class_q_c_p_data_container_qcpdatacontainer-datatype}{QCPData\+Container Data\+Type}{1} documentation for details about this naming convention.    

Implements \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_plottable_interface1_d_acec8492c49e051aaec5ca5267900a98e_acec8492c49e051aaec5ca5267900a98e}{QCPPlottable\+Interface1D}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022}\index{QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}!wheelEvent@{wheelEvent}}
\index{wheelEvent@{wheelEvent}!QCPGraph@{QCPGraph}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{wheelEvent()}{wheelEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022_a47dfd7b8fd99c08ca54e09c362b6f022} 
void QCPLayerable\+::wheel\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QWheel\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user turns the mouse scroll wheel while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3_af524307eacb919827b88233ef7449ce3}{select\+Test}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}.

The {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}angle\+Delta()} indicates how far the mouse wheel was turned, which is usually +/-\/ 120 for single rotation steps. However, if the mouse wheel is turned rapidly, multiple steps may accumulate to one event, making the delta larger. On the other hand, if the wheel has very smooth steps or none at all, the delta may be smaller.

The default implementation does nothing.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}
